[Async-API tutorial](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/)\n\n\n# Asynchronous-API tutorial\n[Contents](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#td-content__toc)\n  *     * [Overview](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#overview)\n    * [Async client](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#async-client)\n    * [Async server](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#async-server)\n      * [Shutting Down the Server](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#shutting-down-the-server)\n\n\n# Asynchronous-API tutorial\nThis tutorial shows you how to write a simple server and client in C++ using gRPC’s asynchronous/non-blocking APIs. It assumes you are already familiar with writing simple synchronous gRPC code, as described in [Basics tutorial](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/basics/). The example used in this tutorial follows from the basic [Greeter example](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/tree/v1.73.0/examples/cpp/helloworld) used in the [quick start](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/quickstart/). You’ll find it along with installation instructions in [grpc/examples/cpp/helloworld](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/tree/v1.73.0/examples/cpp/helloworld).\n### Overview[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#overview)\ngRPC uses the [CompletionQueue](https://grpc.io/grpc/cpp/classgrpc_1_1_completion_queue.html) API for asynchronous operations. The basic work flow is as follows:\n  * bind a `CompletionQueue` to an RPC call\n  * do something like a read or write, present with a unique `void*` tag\n  * call `CompletionQueue::Next` to wait for operations to complete. If a tag appears, it indicates that the corresponding operation is complete.\n\n\n### Async client[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#async-client)\nTo use an asynchronous client to call a remote method, you first create a channel and stub, just as you do in a [synchronous client](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/v1.73.0/examples/cpp/helloworld/greeter_client.cc). Once you have your stub, you do the following to make an asynchronous call:\n  * Initiate the RPC and create a handle for it. Bind the RPC to a `CompletionQueue`.\n```\nCompletionQueue cq;\nstd::unique_ptr<ClientAsyncResponseReader<HelloReply> > rpc(\n  stub_->AsyncSayHello(&context, request, &cq));\n\n```\n\n  * Ask for the reply and final status, with a unique tag\n```\nStatus status;\nrpc->Finish(&reply, &status, (void*)1);\n\n```\n\n  * Wait for the completion queue to return the next tag. The reply and status are ready once the tag passed into the corresponding `Finish()` call is returned.\n```\nvoid* got_tag;\nbool ok = false;\ncq.Next(&got_tag, &ok);\nif (ok && got_tag == (void*)1) {\n // check reply and status\n}\n\n```\n\n\n\nYou can see the complete client example in [greeter_async_client.cc](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/v1.73.0/examples/cpp/helloworld/greeter_async_client.cc).\n### Async server[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#async-server)\nThe server implementation requests an RPC call with a tag and then waits for the completion queue to return the tag. The basic flow for handling an RPC asynchronously is:\n  * Build a server exporting the async service\n```\nhelloworld::Greeter::AsyncService service;\nServerBuilder builder;\nbuilder.AddListeningPort(\"0.0.0.0:50051\", InsecureServerCredentials());\nbuilder.RegisterService(&service);\nauto cq = builder.AddCompletionQueue();\nauto server = builder.BuildAndStart();\n\n```\n\n  * Request one RPC, providing a unique tag\n```\nServerContext context;\nHelloRequest request;\nServerAsyncResponseWriter<HelloReply> responder;\nservice.RequestSayHello(&context, &request, &responder, &cq, &cq, (void*)1);\n\n```\n\n  * Wait for the completion queue to return the tag. The context, request and responder are ready once the tag is retrieved.\n```\nHelloReply reply;\nStatus status;\nvoid* got_tag;\nbool ok = false;\ncq.Next(&got_tag, &ok);\nif (ok && got_tag == (void*)1) {\n // set reply and status\n responder.Finish(reply, status, (void*)2);\n}\n\n```\n\n  * Wait for the completion queue to return the tag. The RPC is finished when the tag is back.\n```\nvoid* got_tag;\nbool ok = false;\ncq.Next(&got_tag, &ok);\nif (ok && got_tag == (void*)2) {\n // clean up\n}\n\n```\n\n\n\nThis basic flow, however, doesn’t take into account the server handling multiple requests concurrently. To deal with this, our complete async server example uses a `CallData` object to maintain the state of each RPC, and uses the address of this object as the unique tag for the call.\n```\nclass CallData {\npublic:\n // Take in the \"service\" instance (in this case representing an asynchronous\n // server) and the completion queue \"cq\" used for asynchronous communication\n // with the gRPC runtime.\n CallData(Greeter::AsyncService* service, ServerCompletionQueue* cq)\n   : service_(service), cq_(cq), responder_(&ctx_), status_(CREATE) {\n  // Invoke the serving logic right away.\n  Proceed();\n }\n void Proceed() {\n  if (status_ == CREATE) {\n   // As part of the initial CREATE state, we *request* that the system\n   // start processing SayHello requests. In this request, \"this\" acts are\n   // the tag uniquely identifying the request (so that different CallData\n   // instances can serve different requests concurrently), in this case\n   // the memory address of this CallData instance.\n   service_->RequestSayHello(&ctx_, &request_, &responder_, cq_, cq_,\n                this);\n   // Make this instance progress to the PROCESS state.\n   status_ = PROCESS;\n  } else if (status_ == PROCESS) {\n   // Spawn a new CallData instance to serve new clients while we process\n   // the one for this CallData. The instance will deallocate itself as\n   // part of its FINISH state.\n   new CallData(service_, cq_);\n   // The actual processing.\n   std::string prefix(\"Hello \");\n   reply_.set_message(prefix + request_.name());\n   // And we are done! Let the gRPC runtime know we've finished, using the\n   // memory address of this instance as the uniquely identifying tag for\n   // the event.\n   responder_.Finish(reply_, Status::OK, this);\n   status_ = FINISH;\n  } else {\n   GPR_ASSERT(status_ == FINISH);\n   // Once in the FINISH state, deallocate ourselves (CallData).\n   delete this;\n  }\n }\n}\n\n```\n\nFor simplicity the server only uses one completion queue for all events, and runs a main loop in `HandleRpcs` to query the queue:\n```\nvoid HandleRpcs() {\n // Spawn a new CallData instance to serve new clients.\n new CallData(&service_, cq_.get());\n void* tag; // uniquely identifies a request.\n bool ok;\n while (true) {\n  // Block waiting to read the next event from the completion queue. The\n  // event is uniquely identified by its tag, which in this case is the\n  // memory address of a CallData instance.\n  cq_->Next(&tag, &ok);\n  GPR_ASSERT(ok);\n  static_cast<CallData*>(tag)->Proceed();\n }\n}\n\n```\n\n#### Shutting Down the Server[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/async/#shutting-down-the-server)\nWe’ve been using a completion queue to get the async notifications. Care must be taken to shut it down _after_ the server has also been shut down.\nRemember we got our completion queue instance `cq_` in `ServerImpl::Run()` by running `cq_ = builder.AddCompletionQueue()`. Looking at `ServerBuilder::AddCompletionQueue`’s documentation we see that\n> … Caller is required to shutdown the server prior to shutting down the returned completion queue.\nRefer to `ServerBuilder::AddCompletionQueue`’s full docstring for more details. What this means in our example is that `ServerImpl's` destructor looks like:\n```\n~ServerImpl() {\n server_->Shutdown();\n // Always shutdown the completion queue after the server.\n cq_->Shutdown();\n}\n\n```\n\nYou can see our complete server example in [greeter_async_server.cc](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/v1.73.0/examples/cpp/helloworld/greeter_async_server.cc).\nLast modified February 17, 2022: [rename RegisterAsyncService to RegisterService (#891) (8f2378a)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/commit/8f2378a66764e8b21f22c6c6f3f1c595c46ec2c9)\n[ View page source](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/tree/main/content/en/docs/languages/cpp/async.md) [ Edit this page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/edit/main/content/en/docs/languages/cpp/async.md) [ Create child page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/new/main/content/en/docs/languages/cpp/async.md?filename=change-me.md&value=---%0Atitle%3A+%22Long+Page+Title%22%0AlinkTitle%3A+%22Short+Nav+Title%22%0Aweight%3A+100%0Adescription%3A+%3E-%0A+++++Page+description+for+heading+and+indexes.%0A---%0A%0A%23%23+Heading%0A%0AEdit+this+template+to+create+your+new+page.%0A%0A%2A+Give+it+a+good+name%2C+ending+in+%60.md%60+-+e.g.+%60getting-started.md%60%0A%2A+Edit+the+%22front+matter%22+section+at+the+top+of+the+page+%28weight+controls+how+its+ordered+amongst+other+pages+in+the+same+directory%3B+lowest+number+first%29.%0A%2A+Add+a+good+commit+message+at+the+bottom+of+the+page+%28%3C80+characters%3B+use+the+extended+description+field+for+more+detail%29.%0A%2A+Create+a+new+branch+so+you+can+preview+your+new+file+and+request+a+review+via+Pull+Request.%0A) [ Create documentation issue](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/issues/new?title=Guides) [ Create project issue](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/issues/new)\n  1. [Docs](https://grpc.io/docs/)\n  2. [Guides](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/)\n\n\n# Guides\nTask-oriented walkthroughs of common use cases\n## [ ](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/#hahahugoshortcode-s0-hbhb)\nThe documentation covers the following techniques:\n##### [Authentication](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/auth/)\nAn overview of gRPC authentication, including built-in auth mechanisms, and how to plug in your own authentication systems.\n##### [Benchmarking](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/benchmarking/)\ngRPC is designed to support high-performance open-source RPCs in many languages. This page describes performance benchmarking tools, scenarios considered by tests, and the testing infrastructure.\n##### [Cancellation](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/cancellation/)\nExplains how and when to cancel RPCs.\n##### [Compression](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/compression/)\nHow to compress the data sent over the wire while using gRPC.\n##### [Custom Backend Metrics](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/custom-backend-metrics/)\nA mechanism in the gRPC library that allows users to inject custom metrics at the gRPC server and consume at gRPC clients to make your custom load balancing algorithms.\n##### [Custom Load Balancing Policies](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/custom-load-balancing/)\nExplains how custom load balancing policies can help optimize load balancing under unique circumstances.\n##### [Custom Name Resolution](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/custom-name-resolution/)\nExplains standard name resolution, the custom name resolver interface, and how to write an implementation.\n##### [Deadlines](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/deadlines/)\nExplains how deadlines can be used to effectively deal with unreliable backends.\n##### [Debugging](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/debugging/)\nExplains the debugging process of gRPC applications using grpcdebug\n##### [Error handling](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/error/)\nHow gRPC deals with errors, and gRPC error codes.\n##### [Flow Control](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/flow-control/)\nExplains what flow control is and how you can manually control it.\n##### [Graceful Shutdown](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/server-graceful-stop/)\nExplains how to gracefully shut down a gRPC server to avoid causing RPC failures for connected clients.\n##### [Health Checking](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/health-checking/)\nExplains how gRPC servers expose a health checking service and how client can be configured to automatically check the health of the server it is connecting to.\n##### [Interceptors](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/interceptors/)\nExplains how interceptors can be used for implementing generic behavior that applies to many RPC methods.\n##### [Keepalive](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/keepalive/)\nHow to use HTTP/2 PING-based keepalives in gRPC.\n##### [Metadata](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/metadata/)\nExplains what metadata is, how it is transmitted, and what it is used for.\n##### [OpenTelemetry Metrics](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/opentelemetry-metrics/)\nOpenTelemetry Metrics available in gRPC\n##### [Performance Best Practices](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/performance/)\nA user guide of both general and language-specific best practices to improve performance.\n##### [Reflection](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/reflection/)\nExplains how reflection can be used to improve the transparency and interpretability of RPCs.\n##### [Request Hedging](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/request-hedging/)\nExplains what request hedging is and how you can configure it.\n##### [Retry](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/retry/)\ngRPC takes the stress out of failures! Get fine-grained retry control and detailed insights with OpenCensus and OpenTelemetry support.\n##### [Service Config](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/service-config/)\nHow the service config can be used by service owners to control client behavior.\n##### [Status Codes](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/status-codes/)\nExplains the status codes used in gRPC.\n##### [Wait-for-Ready](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/wait-for-ready/)\nExplains how to configure RPCs to wait for the server to be ready before sending the request.\nLast modified November 12, 2024: [Embed YouTube videos in different webpages (#1380) (196f408)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/commit/196f408ae74741605fbb66f3ccf23b81fe384667)\n[ View page source](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/tree/main/content/en/docs/guides/_index.md) [ Edit this page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/edit/main/content/en/docs/guides/_index.md) [ Create child page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/new/main/content/en/docs/guides/_index.md?filename=change-me.md&value=---%0Atitle%3A+%22Long+Page+Title%22%0AlinkTitle%3A+%22Short+Nav+Title%22%0Aweight%3A+100%0Adescription%3A+%3E-%0A+++++Page+description+for+heading+and+indexes.%0A---%0A%0A%23%23+Heading%0A%0AEdit+this+template+to+create+your+new+page.%0A%0A%2A+Give+it+a+good+name%2C+ending+in+%60.md%60+-+e.g.+%60getting-started.md%60%0A%2A+Edit+the+%22front+matter%22+section+at+the+top+of+the+page+%28weight+controls+how+its+ordered+amongst+other+pages+in+the+same+directory%3B+lowest+number+first%29.%0A%2A+Add+a+good+commit+message+at+the+bottom+of+the+page+%28%3C80+characters%3B+use+the+extended+description+field+for+more+detail%29.%0A%2A+Create+a+new+branch+so+you+can+preview+your+new+file+and+request+a+review+via+Pull+Request.%0A) [Overview](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#overview)\n    * [gRPC Client with ALTS Transport Security Protocol](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#grpc-client-with-alts-transport-security-protocol)\n    * [gRPC Server with ALTS Transport Security [ALTS](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/)\n\n\n# ALTS authentication\nAn overview of gRPC authentication in C++ using Application Layer Transport Security (ALTS).\n[Contents](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#td-content__toc)\n  *     * [Overview](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#overview)\n    * [gRPC Client with ALTS Transport Security Protocol](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#grpc-client-with-alts-transport-security-protocol)\n    * [gRPC Server with ALTS Transport Security Protocol](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#grpc-server-with-alts-transport-security-protocol)\n    * [Server Authorization](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#server-authorization)\n    * [Client Authorization](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#client-authorization)\n\n\n# ALTS authentication\nAn overview of gRPC authentication in C++ using Application Layer Transport Security (ALTS).\n### Overview[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#overview)\nApplication Layer Transport Security (ALTS) is a mutual authentication and transport encryption system developed by Google. It is used for securing RPC communications within Google’s infrastructure. ALTS is similar to mutual TLS but has been designed and optimized to meet the needs of Google’s production environments. For more information, take a look at the [ALTS whitepaper](https://cloud.google.com/security/encryption-in-transit/application-layer-transport-security).\nALTS in gRPC has the following features:\n  * Create gRPC servers & clients with ALTS as the transport security protocol.\n  * ALTS connections are end-to-end protected with privacy and integrity.\n  * Applications can access peer information such as the peer service account.\n  * Client authorization and server authorization support.\n  * Minimal code changes to enable ALTS.\n\n\ngRPC users can configure their applications to use ALTS as a transport security protocol with few lines of code.\nNote that ALTS is fully functional if the application runs on [Compute Engine](https://cloud.google.com/compute) or [Google Kubernetes Engine (GKE)](https://cloud.google.com/kubernetes-engine).\n### gRPC Client with ALTS Transport Security Protocol[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#grpc-client-with-alts-transport-security-protocol)\ngRPC clients can use ALTS credentials to connect to servers, as illustrated in the following code excerpt:\n```\n#include <grpcpp/grpcpp.h>#include <grpcpp/security/credentials.h>using grpc::experimental::AltsCredentials;\nusing grpc::experimental::AltsCredentialsOptions;\nauto creds = AltsCredentials(AltsCredentialsOptions());\nstd::shared_ptr<grpc::Channel> channel = CreateChannel(server_address, creds);\n\n```\n\n### gRPC Server with ALTS Transport Security Protocol[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#grpc-server-with-alts-transport-security-protocol)\ngRPC servers can use ALTS credentials to allow clients to connect to them, as illustrated next:\n```\n#include <grpcpp/security/server_credentials.h>#include <grpcpp/server.h>#include <grpcpp/server_builder.h>using grpc::experimental::AltsServerCredentials;\nusing grpc::experimental::AltsServerCredentialsOptions;\ngrpc::ServerBuilder builder;\nbuilder.RegisterService(&service);\nauto creds = AltsServerCredentials(AltsServerCredentialsOptions());\nbuilder.AddListeningPort(\"[::]:<port>\", creds);\nstd::unique_ptr<Server> server(builder.BuildAndStart());\n\n```\n\n### Server Authorization[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#server-authorization)\ngRPC has built-in server authorization support using ALTS. A gRPC client using ALTS can set the expected server service accounts prior to establishing a connection. Then, at the end of the handshake, server authorization guarantees that the server identity matches one of the service accounts specified by the client. Otherwise, the connection fails.\n```\n#include <grpcpp/grpcpp.h>#include <grpcpp/security/credentials.h>using grpc::experimental::AltsCredentials;\nusing grpc::experimental::AltsCredentialsOptions;\nAltsCredentialsOptions opts;\nopts.target_service_accounts.push_back(\"expected_server_service_account1\");\nopts.target_service_accounts.push_back(\"expected_server_service_account2\");\nauto creds = AltsCredentials(opts);\nstd::shared_ptr<grpc::Channel> channel = CreateChannel(server_address, creds);\n\n```\n\n### Client Authorization[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/cpp/alts/#client-authorization)\nOn a successful connection, the peer information (e.g., client’s service account) is stored in the [AltsContext](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/gcp/altscontext.proto). gRPC provides a utility library for client authorization check. Assuming that the server knows the expected client identity (e.g., `foo@iam.gserviceaccount.com`), it can run the following example codes to authorize the incoming RPC.\n```\n#include <grpcpp/server_context.h>#include <grpcpp/security/alts_util.h>grpc::ServerContext* context;\ngrpc::Status status = experimental::AltsClientAuthzCheck(\n  context->auth_context(), {\"foo@iam.gserviceaccount.com\"});\n\n```\n\nLast modified August 11, 2021: [Trim trailing whitespace from descriptions (#822) (88d84d6)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/commit/88d84d6536f7dfcc7930050e2734a8fc59e53134)\n[ View page source](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/tree/main/content/en/docs/languages/cpp/alts.md) [ Edit this page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/edit/main/content/en/docs/languages/cpp/alts.md) [ Create child     "https://grpc.io/about": {
      "source_url": "https://grpc.io/about",
      "content": "[gRPC](https://grpc.io/)\n  * [About](https://grpc.io/about/)\n  * [Meet](https://grpc.io/meet/)\n  * [Docs](https://grpc.io/docs/)\n  * [Guides](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/)\n  * [Videos](https://grpc.io/videos/)\n  * [Showcase](https://grpc.io/showcase/)\n  * [Blog](https://grpc.io/blog/)\n  * [Community](https://grpc.io/community/)\n\n\ngRPConf 2025 is on **Aug. 26th!** - [**Register now**](https://events.linuxfoundation.org/grpconf/) ($50 until Jul 30th) or [**Submit a talk proposal**](https://events.linuxfoundation.org/grpconf/program/cfp/) (by May 28th)\n# About gRPC\n### Who is using gRPC and why\n[Contents](https://grpc.io/about/#td-content__toc)\n  *     * [The main usage scenarios](https://grpc.io/about/#the-main-usage-scenarios)\n    * [Core features that make it awesome](https://grpc.io/about/#core-features-that-make-it-awesome)\n  * [Who’s using gRPC and why?](https://grpc.io/about/#whos-using-grpc-and-why)\n  * [The story behind gRPC](https://grpc.io/about/#the-story-behind-grpc)\n\n\ngRPC is a modern open source high performance Remote Procedure Call (RPC) framework that can run in any environment. It can efficiently connect services in and across data centers with pluggable support for load balancing, tracing, health checking and authentication. It is also applicable in last mile of distributed computing to connect devices, mobile applications and browsers to backend services.\n### The main usage scenarios[ ](https://grpc.io/about/#the-main-usage-scenarios)\n  * Efficiently connecting polyglot services in microservices style architecture\n  * Connecting mobile devices, browser clients to backend services\n  * Generating efficient client libraries\n\n\n### Core features that make it awesome[ ](https://grpc.io/about/#core-features-that-make-it-awesome)\n  * Idiomatic client libraries in 11 languages\n  * Highly efficient on wire and with a simple service definition framework\n  * Bi-directional streaming with http/2 based transport\n  * Pluggable auth, tracing, load balancing and health checking\n\n\n## Who’s using gRPC and why?[ ](https://grpc.io/about/#whos-using-grpc-and-why)\nMany companies are already using gRPC for connecting multiple services in their environments. The use case varies from connecting a handful of services to hundreds of services across various languages in on-prem or cloud environments. Below are details and quotes from some of our early adopters.\nCheck out what people are saying below.\n[![Square testimonial logo](https://grpc.io/img/users/square-icon.png)](https://youtu.be/-2sWDr3Z0Wo)\nAt Square, we have been collaborating with Google so that we can replace all uses of our custom RPC solution to use gRPC. We decided to move to gRPC because of its open support for multiple platforms, the demonstrated performance of the protocol, and the ability to customize and adapt it to our network. Developers at Square are looking forward to being able to take advantage of writing streaming APIs and in the future, push gRPC to the edges of the network for integration with mobile clients and third party APIs.\n[![Netflix testimonial logo](https://grpc.io/img/users/netflix-logo.png)](https://github.com/Netflix/ribbon)\nIn our initial use of gRPC we’ve been able to extend it easily to live within our opinionated ecosystem. Further, we’ve had great success making improvements directly to gRPC through pull requests and interactions with Google’s team that manages the project. We expect to see many improvements to developer productivity, and the ability to allow development in non-JVM languages as a result of adopting gRPC.\n[![Cockroach Labs testimonial logo](https://grpc.io/img/users/cockroach-1.png)](https://www.cockroachlabs.com/blog/a-tale-of-two-ports/)\nOur switch from a home-grown RPC system to gRPC was seamless. We quickly took advantage of the per-stream flow control to provide better scheduling of large RPCs over the same connection as small ones.\n[![Cisco testimonial logo](https://grpc.io/img/users/cisco.svg)](https://github.com/CiscoDevNet/grpc-getting-started)\nWith support for high performance bi-directional streaming, TLS based security, and a wide variety of programming languages, gRPC is an ideal unified transport protocol for model driven configuration and telemetry.\n[![Juniper Networks testimonial logo](https://grpc.io/img/users/juniperlogo.png)](https://forums.juniper.net/t5/Automation/OpenConfig-and-gRPC-Junos-Telemetry-Interface/ta-p/316090)\nThe fact that gRPC is built on HTTP/2 transport brings us native bi-directional streaming capabilities and flexible custom-metadata in request headers. The first point is important for large payload-exchange and network-telemetry scenarios, while the latter enables us to expand and include capabilities including but not limited to various network element authentication mechanisms. In addition, the wide language binding support that gRPC/proto3 brings, enables us to provide a flexible and rapid development environment for both internal and external consumers. Last but not least, while there are a number of network communication protocols for configuration, operational state retrieval and network telemetry, gRPC provides us with a unified flexible protocol and transport to ease client/server interaction.\n## The story behind gRPC[ ](https://grpc.io/about/#the-story-behind-grpc)\ngRPC was initially created by Google, which has used a single general-purpose RPC infrastructure called **Stubby** to connect the large number of microservices running within and across its data centers for over a decade. In March 2015, Google decided to build the next version of Stubby and make it open source. The result was gRPC, which is now used in many organizations outside of Google to power use cases from microservices to the “last mile” of computing (mobile, web, and Internet of Things).\nFor more background on why we created gRPC, see the [gRPC Motivation and Design Principles](https://grpc.io/blog/principles/) on the [gRPC blog](https://grpc.io/blog/).\n#### Note\nOur table of **officially supported languages and platforms** has moved! See [Official support](https://grpc.io/docs/#official-support).\n##### Contents\n[ View page source](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/tree/main/content/en/about/_index.md) [ Edit this [Quick start](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/)\n\n\n# Quick start\nThis guide gets you started with gRPC in Dart with a simple working example.\n[Contents](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#td-content__toc)\n  *     * [Prerequisites](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#prerequisites)\n    * [Get the example code](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#get-the-example-code)\n    * [Run the example](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#run-the-example)\n    * [Update the app](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-app)\n      * [Update the gRPC service](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-grpc-service)\n      * [Regenerate gRPC code](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#regenerate-grpc-code)\n      * [Update the server](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-server)\n      * [Update the client](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-client)\n    * [Run the updated app](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#run-the-updated-app)\n    * [Contributing](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#contributing)\n    * [What’s next](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#whats-next)\n\n\n# Quick start\nThis guide gets you started with gRPC in Dart with a simple working example.\n### Prerequisites[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#prerequisites)\n  * **[Dart](https://dart.dev)** version 2.12 or higher, through the Dart or [Flutter](https://flutter.dev) SDKs\nFor installation instructions, see [Install Dart](https://dart.dev/install) or [Install Flutter](https://flutter.dev/docs/get-started/install).\n  * **[Protocol buffer](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers) compiler**, `protoc`, [version 3](https://protobuf.dev/programming-guides/proto3)\nFor installation instructions, see [Protocol Buffer Compiler Installation](https://grpc.io/docs/protoc-installation/).\n  * **Dart plugin** for the protocol compiler:\n    1. Install the protocol compiler plugin for Dart (`protoc-gen-dart`) using the following command:\n```\ndart pub global activate protoc_plugin\n\n```\n\n    2. Update your `PATH` so that the `protoc` compiler can find the plugin:\n```\nexport PATH=\"$PATH:$HOME/.pub-cache/bin\"\n\n```\n\n\n\n#### Note\nDart gRPC supports the Flutter and Server platforms.\n### Get the example code[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#get-the-example-code)\nThe example code is part of the [grpc-dart](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-dart) repo.\n  1. [Download the repo as a zip file](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-dart/archive/master.zip) and unzip it, or clone the repo:\n```\ngit clone https://github.com/grpc/grpc-dart\n\n```\n\n  2. Change to the quick start example directory:\n```\ncd grpc-dart/example/helloworld\n\n```\n\n\n\n### Run the example[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#run-the-example)\nFrom the `example/helloworld` directory:\n  1. Download package dependencies:\n```\ndart pub get\n\n```\n\n  2. Run the server:\n```\ndart bin/server.dart\n\n```\n\n  3. From another terminal, run the client:\n```\ndart bin/client.dart\nGreeter client received: Hello, world!\n\n```\n\n\n\nCongratulations! You’ve just run a client-server application with gRPC.\n### Update the app[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-app)\nIn this section you’ll update the app to make use of an extra server method. The gRPC service is defined using [protocol buffers](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers). To learn more about how to define a service in a `.proto` file, see [Basics tutorial](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/basics/). For now, all you need to know is that both the server and the client stub have a `SayHello()` RPC method that takes a `HelloRequest` parameter from the client and returns a `HelloReply` from the server, and that the method is defined like this:\n```\n// The greeting service definition.\nservice Greeter { // Sends a greeting\n rpc SayHello (HelloRequest) returns (HelloReply) {}}// The request message containing the user's name.\nmessage HelloRequest { string name = 1;}// The response message containing the greetings\nmessage HelloReply { string message = 1;}\n```\n\n#### Update the gRPC service[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-grpc-service)\nOpen `protos/helloworld.proto` and add a new `SayHelloAgain()` method, with the same request and response types:\n```\n// The greeting service definition.\nservice Greeter { // Sends a greeting\n rpc SayHello (HelloRequest) returns (HelloReply) {} // Sends another greeting\n rpc SayHelloAgain (HelloRequest) returns (HelloReply) {}}// The request message containing the user's name.\nmessage HelloRequest { string name = 1;}// The response message containing the greetings\nmessage HelloReply { string message = 1;}\n```\n\nRemember to save the file!\n#### Regenerate gRPC code[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#regenerate-grpc-code)\nBefore you can use the new service method, you need to recompile the updated proto file. From the `example/helloworld` directory, run the following command:\n```\nprotoc --dart_out=grpc:lib/src/generated -Iprotos protos/helloworld.proto\n\n```\n\nYou’ll find the regenerated request and response classes, and client and server classes in the `lib/src/generated` directory.\nNow implement and call the new RPC in the server and client code, respectively.\n#### Update the server[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-server)\nOpen `bin/server.dart` and add the following `sayHelloAgain()` method to the `GreeterService` class:\n```\nclass GreeterService extends GreeterServiceBase {\n @override\n Future<HelloReply> sayHello(ServiceCall call, HelloRequest request) async {\n  return HelloReply()..message = 'Hello, ${request.name}!';\n }\n @override\n Future<HelloReply> sayHelloAgain(ServiceCall call, HelloRequest request) async {\n  return HelloReply()..message = 'Hello again, ${request.name}!';\n }\n}\n\n```\n\n#### Update the client[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#update-the-client)\nAdd a call to `sayHelloAgain()` in `bin/client.dart` like this:\n```\nFuture<void> main(List<String> args) async {\n final channel = ClientChannel(\n  'localhost',\n  port: 50051,\n  options: const ChannelOptions(credentials: ChannelCredentials.insecure()),\n );\n final stub = GreeterClient(channel);\n final name = args.isNotEmpty ? args[0] : 'world';\n try {\n  var response = await stub.sayHello(HelloRequest()..name = name);\n  print('Greeter client received: ${response.message}');\n  response = await stub.sayHelloAgain(HelloRequest()..name = name);\n  print('Greeter client received: ${response.message}');\n } catch (e) {\n  print('Caught error: $e');\n }\n await channel.shutdown();\n}\n\n```\n\n### Run the updated app[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#run-the-updated-app)\nRun the client and server like you did before. Execute the following commands from the `example/helloworld` directory:\n  1. Run the server:\n```\ndart bin/server.dart\n\n```\n\n  2. From another terminal, run the client. This time, add a name as a command-line argument:\n```\ndart bin/client.dart Alice\n\n```\n\nYou’ll see the following output:\n```\nGreeter client received: Hello, Alice!\nGreeter client received: Hello again, Alice!\n\n```\n\n\n\n### Contributing[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#contributing)\nIf you experience problems with Dart gRPC or have a feature request, [create an issue](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-dart/issues/new) over the [grpc-dart](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-dart) repo.\n### What’s next[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/quickstart/#whats-next)\n  * Learn how gRPC works in [Introduction to gRPC](https://grpc.io/docs/what-is-grpc/introduction/) and [Core concepts](https://grpc.io/docs/what-is-grpc/core-concepts/).\n  * Work through the [Basics tutorial](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/basics/).\n  * Explore the [API reference](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/dart/api).\n\n\nLast modified November 25, 2024: [feat: move the $ shell line indicator to scss (#1354) (ab8b3af)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/commit/ab8b3af6ddfccb1995e1a06367593b14972aaf4b)\n[ View page source](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/tree/main/content/en/docs/languages/dart/quickstart.md) [ Edit this page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/edit/main/content/en/docs/languages/dart/quickstart.md) [ Create child page](https://github.com/grpc/grpc.io/new/main/content/en/docs/languages/dart/quickstart.md?filename=change-me.md&value=---%0Atitle%3A+%22Long+Page+Title%22%0AlinkTitle%3A+%22Short+Nav+Title%22%0Aweight%3A+100%0Adescription%3A+%3E-%0A+++++Page+description+for+heading+and+indexes.%0A---%0A%0A%23%23+Heading%0A%0AEdit+this+template+to+create+your+new+page.%0A%0A%2A+Give+it+a+good+name%2C+ending+in+%60.md%60+-+e.g.+%60getting-started.md%60%0A%2A+Edit+the+%22front+matter%22+section+at+the+top+of+the+page+%28weight+controls+how+its+ordered+amongst+other+pages+in+the+same+directory%3B+lowest+number+first%29.%0A%2A+Add+a+good+commit+message+at+the+bottom+of+the+page+%28%3C80+characters%3B+use+the+extended+description+field+for+more+detail%29.%0A%2A+Create+a+new+branch+so+you+can+preview+your+new+file+and+request+a+review+via+Pull+Request.%0A) [Docs](https://grpc.io/docs/)\n\n\n# Documentation\nLearn about key gRPC concepts, try a quick start, find tutorials and reference material for all supported [languages](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/) and [platforms](https://grpc.io/docs/platforms/):\n  * **New to gRPC?** Start with the following pages:\n    * [Introduction to gRPC](https://grpc.io/docs/what-is-grpc/introduction/)\n    * [Core concepts, architecture and lifecycle](https://grpc.io/docs/what-is-grpc/core-concepts/)\n    * [FAQ](https://grpc.io/docs/what-is-grpc/faq/)\n  * **Eager to see gRPC in action?**\nSelect a [language](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/) or [platform](https://grpc.io/docs/platforms/), then choose its **Quick start**.\n  * Interested in **gRPC feature details?**\nTry one of the following:\n    * Select a [language](https://grpc.io/docs/languages/) or [platform](https://grpc.io/docs/platforms/), then choose **Tutorial** or **API reference**\n    * [Guides](https://grpc.io/docs/guides/)\n\n\n### Official support[ ](https://grpc.io/docs/#official-support)\nThese are the officially supported gRPC language, platform and OS versions:\nLanguage| OS| Compilers / SDK  \n---|---|---  \nC/C++| Linux, Mac, Windows| See https://opensource.google/documentation/policies/cplusplus-support  \nC#| Windows, Linux, Mac| .NET Core 3.0+  \nDart| Windows, Linux, Mac| Dart 2.12+  \nGo| Windows, Linux, Mac| Go 1.13+  \nJava| Windows, Linux, Mac| Java 8+ (KitKat+ for Android)  \nKotlin| Windows, Linux, Mac| Kotlin 1.3+  \nNode.js| Windows, Linux, Mac| Node v8+  \nObjective-C| macOS, iOS| See https://opensource.google/documentation/policies/cplusplus-support  \nPHP| Linux, Mac| PHP 7.0+  \nPython| We enforce our [Code of Conduct](https://github.com/cncf/foundation/blob/master/code-of-conduct.md) in all interactions.\n## Stay informed[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#stay-informed)\nBe the first to know! Follow these active channels for timely gRPC announcements:\n[Google Group](https://groups.google.com/g/grpc-io)\nJoin the [grpc-io](https://groups.google.com/g/grpc-io) forum to ask questions and get the latest developer news, including [gRFCs](https://github.com/grpc/proposal).\n[Twitter](https://twitter.com/grpcio)\nFollow us at [@grpcio](https://twitter.com/grpcio) for real-time news on blogs posts, events, and more.\n## Join the conversation[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#join-the-conversation)\nThe [grpc-io](https://groups.google.com/g/grpc-io) forum, mentioned above, is a great place to ask technical questions and engage in discussions with other gRPC developers.\nThe following channels, though less actively monitored, are also good places to exchange with developers and find answers to your gRPC questions:\n[Stack Overflow](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/grpc)\nAsk technical questions about [gRPC](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/grpc) & [protoc,](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/protoc) and find answers.\n### Community meetings[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#community-meetings)\nGet fresh news, and come talk with gRPC developers and other community members at one of our regular online community meetings.\n[Meetup](https://www.meetup.com/gRPCio/)\nMark your [calendars](https://calendar.google.com/calendar/embed?src=c_c6g7cap1fuvdu8m9a3i83lpd7o%40group.calendar.google.com) and join us [online](https://www.meetup.com/gRPCio/) for project updates, live demos, and more.\n[YouTube](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCrnk1HWelWnYtF78YZX80fg)\nMissed a meeting? No problem. Visit the [gRPC channel](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCrnk1HWelWnYtF78YZX80fg) for meeting videos.\n## Contribute[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#contribute)\n### gRPC code and documentation[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#grpc-code-and-documentation)\nInterested in contributing to gRPC code or documentation found under the [grpc](https://github.com/grpc) GitHub organization? To learn how, read [grpc-community/CONTRIBUTING.md](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-community/blob/main/CONTRIBUTING.md) and the `CONTRIBUTING.md` page of the repo that you’d like to contribute to.\n### gRPC Ecosystem[ ](https://grpc.io/community/#grpc-ecosystem)\nThe [gRPC Ecosystem](https://github.com/grpc-ecosystem) is a GitHub organization that hosts community projects related to gRPC — projects include, but are not limited to, gRPC extensions or integrations, as well as examples that demonstrate how to use gRPC for common or technically challenging use cases.\nDo you have a gRPC-related project that’s a good candidate for the ecosystem? Core \nThe GRPC Core library is a low-level library designed to be wrapped by higher level libraries. The top-level API is provided in [grpc.h](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/cpp/grpc_8h.html). The bind method is typically generated code and is used to register a service's methods with the server on startup.\nThe bind method signature takes a [ServiceBinderBase](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ServiceBinderBase.html) and an optional instance of the service base class, e.g. `static void BindService(ServiceBinderBase, GreeterService)`.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#callcredentials)[CallCredentials](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.CallCredentials.html)\nClient-side call credentials. Most users will use this class only indirectly and will be making calls using client object generated from protocol buffer definition files.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#channel)[Channel](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.Channel.html)\nRepresents a gRPC channel. Channels are an abstraction of long-lived connections to remote servers. More client objects can reuse the same channel. Creating a channel is an expensive operation compared to invoking a remote call so in general you should reuse a single channel for as many calls as possible.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#channelbase)[ChannelBase](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ChannelBase.html)\nBase class for gRPC channel. In situations when a backend is making calls to another backend, it makes sense to propagate properties like deadline and cancellation token of the server call to the child call. Underlying gRPC implementation may provide other \"opaque\" contexts (like tracing context) that are not explicitly accesible via the public C# API, but this token still allows propagating them.\n#### exchanged during a call. gRPC supports these types of metadata: \n  * Request headersare sent by the client at the beginning of a remote call before any request messages are sent.\n  * Response headersare sent by the server at the beginning of a remote call handler before any response messages are sent.\n  * Response trailersare sent by the server at the end of a remote call along with resulting call status.\n\n\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#metadata-entry)[Metadata.Entry](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.Metadata.Entry.html)\nMetadata See <https://codingforsmarties.wordpress.com/2016/01/21/how-to-version-assemblies-destined-for-nuget/> for rationale about assembly versioning.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#writeoptions)[WriteOptions](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.WriteOptions.html)\nOptions for write operations.\n### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#structs)Structs \n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#callinvocationdetails-trequest-tresponse)[CallInvocationDetails<TRequest, TResponse>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.CallInvocationDetails-2.html)\nDetails about a client-side call to be invoked.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#calloptions)[CallOptions](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.CallOptions.html)\nOptions for calls made by client.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#status)[Status](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.Status.html)\nRepresents RPC result, which consists of [StatusCode](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.Status.html#Grpc_Core_Status_StatusCode) and an optional detail string.\n### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#interfaces)Interfaces \n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#iasyncstreamreader-t)[IAsyncStreamReader<T>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.IAsyncStreamReader-1.html)\nA stream of messages to be read. Messages can be awaited `await reader.MoveNext()`, that returns `true` if there is a message available and `false` if there are no more messages (i.e. the stream has been closed). \nOn the client side, the last invocation of `MoveNext()` either returns `false` if the call has finished successfully or throws `RpcException` if call finished with an error. Once the call finishes, subsequent invocations of `MoveNext()` will continue yielding the same result (returning `false` or throwing an exception). \nOn the server side, `MoveNext()` does not throw exceptions. In case of a failure, the request stream will appear to be finished (`MoveNext` will return `false`) and the `CancellationToken` associated with the call will be cancelled to signal the failure. \n`MoveNext()` operations can be cancelled via a cancellation token. Cancelling an individual read operation has the same effect as cancelling the entire call (which will also result in the read operation returning prematurely), but the per-read cancellation tokens passed to MoveNext() only result in cancelling the call if the read operation haven't finished yet. \n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#iasyncstreamwriter-t)[IAsyncStreamWriter<T>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.IAsyncStreamWriter-1.html)\nA writable stream of messages.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#iclientstreamwriter-t)[IClientStreamWriter<T>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.IClientStreamWriter-1.html)\nClient-side writable stream of messages with Close capability.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#imethod)[IMethod](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.IMethod.html)\nA non-generic representation of a remote method.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#iserverstreamwriter-t)[IServerStreamWriter<T>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.IServerStreamWriter-1.html)\nA writable stream of messages that is used in server-side handlers.\n### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#enums)Enums \n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#channeloption-optiontype)[ChannelOption.OptionType](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ChannelOption.OptionType.html)\nType of `ChannelOption`.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#channelstate)[ChannelState](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ChannelState.html)\nConnectivity state of a channel. Based on grpc_connectivity_state from grpc/grpc.h\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#compressionlevel)[CompressionLevel](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.CompressionLevel.html)\nCompression level based on grpc_compression_level from grpc/compression.h\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#methodtype)[MethodType](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.MethodType.html)\nMethod types supported by gRPC.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#sslclientcertificaterequesttype)[SslClientCertificateRequestType](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.SslClientCertificateRequestType.html)\nModes of requesting client's SSL certificate by the server. Corresponds to `grpc_ssl_client_certificate_request_type`.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#statuscode)[StatusCode](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.StatusCode.html)\nResult of a remote procedure call. Based on grpc_status_code from grpc/status.h\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#writeflags)[WriteFlags](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.WriteFlags.html)\nFlags for write operations.\n### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#delegates)Delegates \n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#asyncauthinterceptor)[AsyncAuthInterceptor](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.AsyncAuthInterceptor.html)\nAsynchronous authentication interceptor for [CallCredentials](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.CallCredentials.html).\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#clientstreamingservermethod-trequest-tresponse)[ClientStreamingServerMethod<TRequest, TResponse>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ClientStreamingServerMethod-2.html)\nServer-side handler for client streaming call.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#duplexstreamingservermethod-trequest-tresponse)[DuplexStreamingServerMethod<TRequest, TResponse>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.DuplexStreamingServerMethod-2.html)\nServer-side handler for bidi streaming call.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#serverstreamingservermethod-trequest-tresponse)[ServerStreamingServerMethod<TRequest, TResponse>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.ServerStreamingServerMethod-2.html)\nServer-side handler for server streaming call.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#unaryservermethod-trequest-tresponse)[UnaryServerMethod<TRequest, TResponse>](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.UnaryServerMethod-2.html)\nServer-side handler for unary call.\n#### [](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#verifypeercallback)[VerifyPeerCallback](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core.VerifyPeerCallback.html)\nCallback invoked with the expected targetHost and the peer's certificate. If false is returned by this callback then it is treated as a verification failure and the attempted connection will fail. Invocation of the callback is blocking, so any implementation should be light-weight. Note that the callback can potentially be invoked multiple times, concurrently from different threads (e.g. when multiple connections are being created for the same credentials).\n##### In This Article\n  * [Classes ](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#classes)\n  * [Structs ](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#structs)\n  * [Interfaces ](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#interfaces)\n  * [Enums ](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#enums)\n  * [Delegates ](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#delegates)\n\n\n[Back to top](https://grpc.github.io/grpc/csharp/api/Grpc.Core#top) Generated by **DocFX**\n",

It can efficiently connect services in and across data centers with pluggable support for load balancing, tracing, health checking and authentication. It is also applicable in last mile of distributed computing to connect devices, mobile applications and browsers to backend services.\n![Simple service definition feature icon](https://grpc.io/img/icons/feature-1.svg)\n### Simple service definition\nDefine your service using Protocol Buffers, a powerful binary serialization toolset and language\n![Start quickly and scale feature icon](https://grpc.io/img/icons/feature-2.svg)\n### Start quickly and scale\nInstall runtime and dev environments with a single line and also scale to millions of RPCs per second with the framework\n![Works across languages and platforms feature icon](https://grpc.io/img/icons/feature-3.svg)\n### Works across languages and platforms\nAutomatically generate idiomatic client and server stubs for your service in a variety of languages and platforms\n![Bi-directional streaming and integrated auth feature icon](https://grpc.io/img/icons/feature-4.svg)\n### Bi-directional streaming and integrated auth\nBi-directional streaming and fully integrated pluggable authentication with HTTP/2-based transport\n## Used by\n[![Square
